      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n18360-4" target="مُزَاوَجَةٌ" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n18357"/></foreign> (S, A, K) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n18360-5" target="تَزَاوُجٌ" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> (S) are syn.: (S, A, * K:) <foreign lang="ar">ازدواج</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">A conformity,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">mutual resemblance,</hi> [<hi rend="ital">with respect to sound,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">measure,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">of two words occurring near together;</hi> as in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ سَبَأٍ بِنَبَأٍ</foreign> [in the Kur xxvii. 22]: (Kull p. 31:) and this is also termed   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n18360-6" target="مُزَاوَجَةٌ" n="6" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n18357"/></foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مُحَاذَاةٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مُوَازَنَةٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مُقَابَلَةٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مُؤَازَاةٌ</foreign>. (Marginal note in a copy of the Muzhir, 22nd <foreign lang="ar">نوع</foreign>.)    </entryFree>29:T43a,<entryFree id="n18361" key="زَاجٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">زَاجٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> [<hi rend="ital">Vitriol;</hi>] <hi rend="ital">a well-known kind of salt;</hi> (K, TA;) <hi rend="ital">called</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">شَبٌّ يَمَانِىٌّ</foreign>; [but see <foreign lang="ar">شَبٌّ</foreign>;] <hi rend="ital">which is a medicinal substance, and one of the ingredients of ink:</hi> (Lth, TA:) [pl. <foreign lang="ar">زَاجَاتٌ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">species,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">sorts, of vitriol;</hi> namely, green, or sulphate of iron, which is an ingredient in ink, and is generally meant by the term <foreign lang="ar">زاج</foreign> when unrestricted by an epithet; blue, or sulphate of copper; and white, or sulphate of zinc:] it is a Pers. word, (S,) arabicized, (S, K,) originally <foreign lang="ar">زاگ</foreign>. (TA.)    </entryFree>2a:T2c04,<entryFree id="n18362" key="زَوْجٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">زَوْجٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> primarily signifies <hi rend="ital">A sort of thing of any kind</hi> [<hi rend="ital">that is one of a pair</hi> or <hi rend="ital">couple</hi>]: and <foreign lang="ar">زَوْجَانِ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">a pair,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">couple,</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">any two things paired</hi> or <hi rend="ital">coupled together,</hi> whether they be <hi rend="ital">likes</hi> or <hi rend="ital">contraries:</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">زَوْجٌ</foreign> signifying <hi rend="ital">either one of such two things:</hi> (Az, TA:) or, accord. to 'Alee Ibn- 'Eesà, <hi rend="ital">a sort of thing</hi> [absolutely]: (Mgh:) or <hi rend="ital">a sort of thing having its like,</hi> (El-Ghooree, Mgh, Msb,) as in the case of species; (Msb;) or <hi rend="ital">having its contrary,</hi> (El-Ghooree, Mgh, Msb,) as the moist and the dry, and the male and the female, and the night and the day, and the bitter and the sweet; (Msb;) though sometimes applied to <hi rend="ital">any sort of thing;</hi> and to <hi rend="ital">a single thing:</hi> (El-Ghooree, Mgh:) or it is applied to <hi rend="ital">a single thing</hi> only when <hi rend="ital">having with it a thing of the same kind;</hi> (Mgh, Msb;) <foreign lang="ar">زَوْجَانِ</foreign> signifying <hi rend="ital">a pair,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">couple, of such things:</hi> (Mgh:) the pl. is <foreign lang="ar">أَزْوَاجِ</foreign>: (TA:) you say <foreign lang="ar">زَوْجَانِ مِنْ حَمَامٍ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">زَوْجَا حَمَامٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">A pair</hi> 
                  <pb n="1267"/> 
                  <hi rend="ital">of pigeons</hi>]: (A:) and <foreign lang="ar">اِشْتَرَيْتُ زَوْجَى حَمَامٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I bought a pair of pigeons</hi>], meaning a male and a female: (S:) and <foreign lang="ar">زَوْجَا نِعَالٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">A pair of sandals</hi>]: (S, A:) and in like manner <foreign lang="ar">زَوْجَيْنِ</foreign> is used in the Kur xi. 42 and xxiii. 28; (S;) meaning a male and a female: (Bd, Jel:) or, accord. to the M, <foreign lang="ar">زَوْجٌ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">one of a pair</hi> or <hi rend="ital">couple:</hi> and also <hi rend="ital">a pair</hi> or <hi rend="ital">couple together:</hi> (TA:) and in like manner says AO, (Mgh, Msb,) and IKt, and IF: (Msb:) and ISh says that it signifies <hi rend="ital">two;</hi> (Mgh;) and so says IDrd: (Msb:) so that you say, <foreign lang="ar">هُمَا زَوْجٌ</foreign> as well as <foreign lang="ar">هُمَا زَوْجَانِ</foreign> [meaning <hi rend="ital">They two are a pair,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">couple</hi>]; (S, K, TA;) like as you say, <foreign lang="ar">هُمَا سَوَآءٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">هُمَا سِيَّانِ</foreign>: (S, TA:) and <foreign lang="ar">عِنْدِى زَوْجُ نِعَالٍ</foreign>, meaning [<hi rend="ital">I have</hi>] <hi rend="ital">two</hi> [<hi rend="ital">sandals</hi>]; and <foreign lang="ar">زَوْجَانِ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">four:</hi> (Msb:) or <foreign lang="ar">زَوْجُ حَمَامٍ</foreign> as meaning a male and a female [of pigeons] is a phrase which should not be used; one to which the vulgar are addicted: (TA:) IAmb says, the vulgar are wrong in thinking that <foreign lang="ar">زَوْجٌ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">two;</hi> for the Arabs used not to employ such a phrase as <foreign lang="ar">زَوْجُ حَمَامٍ</foreign>, but used to say <foreign lang="ar">زَوْجَانِ مِنَ الحَمَامِ</foreign>, (Mgh, Msb, TA,) meaning a male and a female; (TA;) and <foreign lang="ar">زَوْجَانِ مِنَ الخِفَافِ</foreign>, (Mgh, Msb, TA,) meaning the right and the left [of boots]: (TA:) nor did they apply the term <foreign lang="ar">زَوْجٌ</foreign> to <hi rend="ital">one</hi> of birds, like as they applied the dual, <foreign lang="ar">زَوْجَانِ</foreign>, to <hi rend="ital">two;</hi> but they applied the term <foreign lang="ar">فَرْدٌ</foreign> to the male, and <foreign lang="ar">فَرْدَةٌ</foreign> to the female: (Mgh, Msb:) Es-Sijistánee, also, says that the term <foreign lang="ar">زَوْجٌ</foreign> should not be applied to <hi rend="ital">two,</hi> neither of birds nor of other things, for this is a usage of the ignorant; but to every two, <foreign lang="ar">زَوْجَانِ</foreign>: (Msb:) Az says that the grammarians disapprove the saying of ISh that <foreign lang="ar">زَوْجٌ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">two</hi> of any things, (Mgh, * TA,) and that <foreign lang="ar">زَوْجَانِ مِنْ خِفَافٍ</foreign> signifies [<hi rend="ital">Two pairs of boots,</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">four</hi> [<hi rend="ital">boots</hi>]; (TA:) in the Kur xxii. 5 and 1. 7 [it seems to be implied that it means <hi rend="ital">pair</hi> or <hi rend="ital">couple;</hi> but more probably in these instances] it means <hi rend="ital">sort,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">species:</hi> (Bd, Jel:) it is also expl. by the word <foreign lang="ar">لَوْنٌ</foreign> [used in this last sense]: (T, TA;) in the Kur xxxviii. 58, its pl. <foreign lang="ar">أَزْوَاجٌ</foreign> means <foreign lang="ar">أَلْوَانٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">أَنْوَاعٌ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">sorts,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">species</hi>] of punishment: F explains the sing. as meaning <foreign lang="ar">لَوْنٌ مِنَ الدِّيبَاجِ وَنَحْوِهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">a sort,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">species, of silk brocade and the like</hi>];
